Does Opus 4.7 forget the news? A fully transparent empirical investigation — document parsing first, then knowledge recall

By Tomasz Kolinko · April 17, 2026 · 137 tests across 6 batteries, ~340 model answers, every question exposed for scrutiny

A friend (Arvind) observed that Opus 4.7 appeared to regress on news date handling in his multi-agent research system — "dropped to Sonnet level," specifically mixing up months. His use case is feeding documents to Claude/Opus for parsing. This report tests that claim empirically across 6 test batteries, with document parsing prioritized since that matches his workflow.

"Ważne! Opus 4.7 nie ogarnia dat newsów i aktualizacji tak jak robił to 4.6. To jest core quality modelu dla wielu moich rzeczy więc sprawdziłem i nowy Opus spadł do jakości Sonneta w tej konkretnej kwestii." "Important! Opus 4.7 doesn't handle news dates and updates as well as 4.6 did. This is core quality for many of my use cases — the new Opus dropped to Sonnet-level quality."
Revised verdict: nuanced / partially supported. Document parsing (the use case Arvind described): 4.7 ~ 4.6, both above Sonnet. Pure training recall: 4.7 slightly above 4.6. Month precision on recall only: 4.7 slightly below 4.6 (86.7% vs 93.1%). No single metric shows "Sonnet level" collapse. See document parsing section first — that's where his actual workflow lives.
Jump to 1. Document parsing (priority)   ↳ Hard parsing   ↳ Month precision in parsing 2. Month precision (recall) 3. Broad knowledge recall

Methodology

  • Document parsing tests (hard + month-parsing, 52 questions): Real or synthetic documents fed to models, deterministic scoring (no LLM judge). Expected answer derived from the document itself.
  • Month recall test (30 questions): "In which month did X happen?" — deterministic scoring.
  • Broad knowledge tests (55 questions across 4 batteries): mixed questions graded 0-10 by a blinded Claude Opus judge (outputs labeled X/Y/Z, presentation order randomized per test). Zero model-identity leaks in any output.
  • All tests: pure API (no tools, no system prompt), single shot per question.
  • Previously corrected: 2 test criteria I wrote wrong (gpt-4.5-release, wiki-2024-events) — all 3 models got full credit after re-scoring.

1. Document parsing (Arvind's use case)

These are the tests closest to the multi-agent research use case: give the model a document, ask it to extract/count/reason about dates. Deterministic scoring: the answer is in the document, so correctness is unambiguous.

Pooled summary

ModelCorrectUnder-count errorsOver-count errorsAccuracy
opus-4.646/523388.5%
opus-4.746/524288.5%
sonnet-4.644/525284.6%

Both Opus versions tie (~89% accuracy), both above Sonnet (~83%). 4.7 undercounts slightly more often than 4.6 — the specific failure mode matching Arvind's observation — but not enough to drop to Sonnet level.

Hard document parsing (27 Q)

Stress-tests: long docs (3000+ chars), distractors, ambiguous date formats, European vs US conventions, exclusion filters, cross-section aggregation.

ModelCorrectAdjacent (±1)Close (±2-3)FarRefusedAccuracy
opus-4.621/27231077.8%
opus-4.722/27410081.5%
sonnet-4.619/27430170.4%

How many distinct AI model/system releases or announcements happened in March 2025 according to this news feed? Include: Apple visionOS 2.4, GPT-5 announce, Gemini 2.5 Pro, Llama 4 preview. Exclude court rulings and acquisitions and EU AI Act milestones. Just the number.

Document provided (3308 chars)

AGGREGATED NEWS FEED — March 20, 2025

This week's selected headlines (in no particular order):

"Senate confirms new FTC chair on March 4, 2025" — Reuters
The Senate confirmed Lina Khan's successor on March 4, replacing the
previous chair who had served since 2021. The confirmation vote was 52-48
along party lines. The new chair's priorities include reviewing the
2024 consolidation wave.

"Apple releases visionOS 2.4" — The Verge
Apple pushed visionOS 2.4 to the Vision Pro on the 18th of March, 2025,
adding Apple Intelligence features first previewed at WWDC 2024 (held in
June of that year). This follows visionOS 2.3, which shipped in late
January 2025 (specifically January 27).

"GPT-5 Announced" — OpenAI blog
OpenAI announced GPT-5 on 2025-03-15, with public availability planned for
"late Q2 2025." A research preview opens April 1 for Tier 5 developers.
OpenAI's previous major release was GPT-4o, which launched in May 2024.

"Google releases Gemini 2.5 Pro" — Google blog, dated Mar. 12, 2025
Gemini 2.5 Pro was released March 12, 2025, three months after the
December 11, 2024 release of Gemini 2.0 Flash. The 2.0 Pro was skipped
for direct-to-2.5 jump.

"EU AI Act compliance deadline" — EuActiv
The first major compliance milestone of the EU AI Act is February 2,
2025 (prohibited AI practices ban), though enforcement activity has been
limited in the weeks since. The next milestone is August 2, 2025 (general-
purpose AI governance), and full applicability arrives August 2, 2026.

"Anthropic publishes Claude 3.7 safety card" — Anthropic
The safety card for Claude 3.7 Sonnet was published on February 24, 2025,
two days after the model's release. This release broke Anthropic's usual
cadence — Claude 3.5 Sonnet had shipped 20 June 2024, with the "new" 3.5
on 22 October 2024, and 3.5 Haiku on the fourth of November, 2024.

"Meta announces Llama 4 research preview" — Meta AI blog
On Mar 10, 2025, Meta announced that Llama 4 research samples were
available. Full release is "coming this summer." This follows Llama 3.3,
released December 6, 2024, and Llama 3.2, which had launched September
25, 2024.

"Microsoft acquires [REDACTED] for $2.5B" — WSJ, 3/17/2025 [US format]
Microsoft announced the acquisition of [REDACTED] on March 17, 2025.
This is Microsoft's largest AI acquisition since their $4B investment in
a major European AI lab (announced 2023-09-12, closed Dec 2023).

"xAI releases Grok 3" — xAI blog
xAI announced Grok 3 on February 17, 2025. This is their third major
release, following Grok 2 on August 14, 2024, and the original Grok on
November 3, 2023.

"Mistral releases Mistral Small 3" — Mistral AI
Mistral Small 3 was released 2025-01-30. This is Mistral's third major
release of 2025 so far — after the previous minor Mistral updates in
January and a small update in early February that mostly fixed bugs.

"Court ruling on AI training data" — Bloomberg Law
A federal judge ruled on March 19, 2025 that the training data in the
Smith v. BigLab case was fair use. The lawsuit had been filed in
June 2023 and went to trial in January 2025.

"Amazon launches Nova models" — AWS re:Invent 2024 recap
Amazon's Nova family (Micro, Lite, Pro, Premier) launched at re:Invent
2024, which ran December 2-6, 2024. The models went GA shortly after,
on January 15, 2025.

Question asked

In which month did Amazon Nova go GA (general availability)? Just the month.

Document provided (3308 chars)

AGGREGATED NEWS FEED — March 20, 2025

This week's selected headlines (in no particular order):

"Senate confirms new FTC chair on March 4, 2025" — Reuters
The Senate confirmed Lina Khan's successor on March 4, replacing the
previous chair who had served since 2021. The confirmation vote was 52-48
along party lines. The new chair's priorities include reviewing the
2024 consolidation wave.

"Apple releases visionOS 2.4" — The Verge
Apple pushed visionOS 2.4 to the Vision Pro on the 18th of March, 2025,
adding Apple Intelligence features first previewed at WWDC 2024 (held in
June of that year). This follows visionOS 2.3, which shipped in late
January 2025 (specifically January 27).

"GPT-5 Announced" — OpenAI blog
OpenAI announced GPT-5 on 2025-03-15, with public availability planned for
"late Q2 2025." A research preview opens April 1 for Tier 5 developers.
OpenAI's previous major release was GPT-4o, which launched in May 2024.

"Google releases Gemini 2.5 Pro" — Google blog, dated Mar. 12, 2025
Gemini 2.5 Pro was released March 12, 2025, three months after the
December 11, 2024 release of Gemini 2.0 Flash. The 2.0 Pro was skipped
for direct-to-2.5 jump.

"EU AI Act compliance deadline" — EuActiv
The first major compliance milestone of the EU AI Act is February 2,
2025 (prohibited AI practices ban), though enforcement activity has been
limited in the weeks since. The next milestone is August 2, 2025 (general-
purpose AI governance), and full applicability arrives August 2, 2026.

"Anthropic publishes Claude 3.7 safety card" — Anthropic
The safety card for Claude 3.7 Sonnet was published on February 24, 2025,
two days after the model's release. This release broke Anthropic's usual
cadence — Claude 3.5 Sonnet had shipped 20 June 2024, with the "new" 3.5
on 22 October 2024, and 3.5 Haiku on the fourth of November, 2024.

"Meta announces Llama 4 research preview" — Meta AI blog
On Mar 10, 2025, Meta announced that Llama 4 research samples were
available. Full release is "coming this summer." This follows Llama 3.3,
released December 6, 2024, and Llama 3.2, which had launched September
25, 2024.

"Microsoft acquires [REDACTED] for $2.5B" — WSJ, 3/17/2025 [US format]
Microsoft announced the acquisition of [REDACTED] on March 17, 2025.
This is Microsoft's largest AI acquisition since their $4B investment in
a major European AI lab (announced 2023-09-12, closed Dec 2023).

"xAI releases Grok 3" — xAI blog
xAI announced Grok 3 on February 17, 2025. This is their third major
release, following Grok 2 on August 14, 2024, and the original Grok on
November 3, 2023.

"Mistral releases Mistral Small 3" — Mistral AI
Mistral Small 3 was released 2025-01-30. This is Mistral's third major
release of 2025 so far — after the previous minor Mistral updates in
January and a small update in early February that mostly fixed bugs.

"Court ruling on AI training data" — Bloomberg Law
A federal judge ruled on March 19, 2025 that the training data in the
Smith v. BigLab case was fair use. The lawsuit had been filed in
June 2023 and went to trial in January 2025.

"Amazon launches Nova models" — AWS re:Invent 2024 recap
Amazon's Nova family (Micro, Lite, Pro, Premier) launched at re:Invent
2024, which ran December 2-6, 2024. The models went GA shortly after,
on January 15, 2025.

Expected answer & rationale

Expected: January
Notes: 'on January 15, 2025'

purpose AI governance), and full applicability arrives August 2, 2026.

COMPANY HISTORY — CONFIDENTIAL INTERNAL DOCUMENT
Compiled by the Office of the CEO, last revised 2026-02-14

--- Founding Era (2019-2021) ---

Our company was incorporated in Delaware on the third of September, 2019, though
the founding team had actually been working together since the summer of that
year. The initial idea sketched out at a whiteboard session in late August led
to a seed round closing on 15/11/2019 (European format throughout this European-
origin document unless otherwise marked [US]). Angel investors contributed
$750K. The corporate structure was finalized the following quarter.

A first product prototype shipped on 22 January 2020, four months before COVID
locked down Europe. The pandemic paradoxically accelerated us — we closed our
Series A on 8/6/2020 (eight of June), raising €4.2M led by Index Ventures.
Revenue ramp began in earnest the month after that round closed. By the end of
Q3 2020 we had 14 paying customers.

The second product launched on 11/11/2020, coincidentally Armistice Day. The
team grew to 22 people by year end. An early office move happened in February
of the following year — specifically 2021-02-19. The office warming party on
Friday 26 February 2021 was the last in-person event for six months.

--- Growth Era (2021-2023) ---

A pivotal hire was CTO Anna Kubasiak, who joined on the twelfth of April 2021,
having given notice at her previous employer in early March. Under her,
engineering grew from 7 to 24 people by the end of 2021.

Series B closed on 2022-01-10 — €18M at a €120M valuation, Accel-led. The
announcement was made public on 17/1/2022, a week after signing. We had a bad
week in March 2022 (the Ukraine war began, remote team in Kyiv had to relocate)
but by the end of Q2 2022 headcount recovery was complete.

Two major product releases in 2022: the flagship v3 platform on 14 June 2022
and the mobile apps on Oct 3, 2022 [US date format, from our US PR agency
press release]. Year-end revenue hit €22M ARR.

The first major downturn hit in Q1 2023. Layoffs affecting 23% of the team
were announced on 2023-03-08 (international women's day, terrible timing) and
completed by the end of that month. We paused hiring entirely for six months
— specifically through the end of September 2023.

--- Recovery and IPO Prep (2024-2025) ---

Hiring resumed in October 2023, cautiously at first. A big turning point was
the Llama 3 integration shipping on 2024-04-18, which unlocked a new enterprise
segment. Series C followed on June 5, 2024 [US format] — €40M at a €400M
valuation. This round was announced externally on the twentieth of June 2024.

Revenue crossed €50M ARR in August 2024 (specifically by the 22nd). The EU
regulatory filing (required for public listing) was submitted on 12/12/2024.

The IPO was priced on 3/4/2025 [this doc uses European format — so April 3,
2025] and began trading the following week. Opening was stronger than expected.
By the end of the first trading month (end of April), we had gained 38% from
the IPO price.

The most recent all-hands presentation was the thirty-first of January 2026,
exactly two weeks before this document was revised.

ACME Corp Q3 2024 Earnings Report
Filed: October 28, 2024

REVENUE TIMELINE:
Jul '24: $12.3M (up 15% QoQ)
Aug-24: $14.1M (new customer wins)
09/2024: $15.8M (record quarter close)

KEY EVENTS DURING Q3:
- Product launch on July 11th: new Enterprise tier
- Acquisition announced August 22, 2024: DataFlow Inc. for $50M
- Partnership signed Sep 18: Microsoft channel agreement
- CEO change effective October 1 (post-quarter)

GUIDANCE (Q4 2024):
Expecting revenue between $45-50M, continuing momentum from 
strong bookings in the quarter ending September 30, 2024.
Earlier forward guidance issued in April 2024 projected $42M, 
which we have exceeded.

YEAR-AGO COMPARISON:
Q3 2023 revenue was $28.4M (vs current $42.2M), with most growth
happening after the September 2023 product refresh.

MANAGEMENT NOTES:
The period April-June 2024 represented the inflection point for our 
Enterprise strategy, with May 2024 alone accounting for 3 of our 
top-10 deals ever. We expect this momentum to continue through 
December 2024 and into Q1 2025.

Document provided (1286 chars)

TECH NEWS DIGEST

Recent Developments in AI (late 2024):

The AI landscape saw significant movement throughout the second half of 2024.
OpenAI kicked things off with their release of GPT-4o on May 13, 2024, marking
a major step forward in multimodal capabilities. 

By June 20th, Anthropic responded with Claude 3.5 Sonnet, which quickly became
a favorite among developers for its strong coding ability. Just over a month
later, on July 23, Meta released Llama 3.1, including a 405-billion-parameter
variant.

The fall brought a rapid cadence of updates. OpenAI announced o1-preview on
September 12, 2024, introducing the reasoning-model paradigm. Anthropic
followed with Claude 3.5 Sonnet (New) on 2024-10-22, bringing "computer use"
capabilities.

November saw Anthropic release Claude 3.5 Haiku (November 4th) and introduce
the Model Context Protocol (MCP) late in the month (November 25). Meta also
released Llama 3.3 during this period, on the 6th of December, 2024.

The year closed with OpenAI's "12 Days" event, starting December 5, 2024 and
running through the 20th. Google released Gemini 2.0 Flash in experimental
form on 11 Dec 2024. DeepSeek then shocked the industry with V3 on
December 26, 2024, demonstrating that smaller Chinese labs could match
frontier capabilities.

Reading the month-recall results:

  • 4.7 had 4 month errors; 4.6 and Sonnet each had 2
  • Only 4.7 produced a "far" error (said June for Meta Quest 3, actually October — 4 months off)
  • 4.7 answered all questions while 4.6 and Sonnet each refused one — 4.7 is more willing to answer confidently, sometimes wrong
  • 4.7 attempted accuracy: 86.7% vs 93.1% for 4.6 and Sonnet
  • This is the narrowest metric showing 4.7 regression. On broader or document-parsing tasks, 4.7 matches or exceeds 4.6.

# 12 Days of OpenAI

The **"12 Days of OpenAI"** (also sometimes called "Shipmas") was a series of daily product announcements and livestreams that OpenAI held over 12 consecutive weekdays in **December 2024**, starting on **December 5, 2024**.

Each day, OpenAI revealed a new product, feature, or update. Some of the notable announcements included:

- **Full o1 model** release and ChatGPT Pro ($200/month subscription tier)
- **Sora** (their video generation model) public launch
- **Canvas** features for ChatGPT
- **ChatGPT Projects** for organizing conversations
- **Advanced Voice Mode** expansions (including Santa voice and video/screen sharing capabilities)
- **ChatGPT Search** expansion
- **o3** model preview (announced on the final day)

The event was led by CEO **Sam Altman** and other OpenAI team members, with daily livestreams typically broadcast on YouTube and other platforms. It was widely seen as a major marketing push to showcase the breadth of OpenAI's work heading into the end of the year.

I should note that my knowledge has limits on some specifics, so a few details above may be slightly off, but this captures the general picture of the event.

## OpenAI's 12 Days of OpenAI

The **12 Days of OpenAI** was a series of live announcements and product reveals that OpenAI held over 12 consecutive weekdays. It took place in **December 2024**, running from **December 5 through December 20, 2024**.

Each day featured a livestreamed announcement, often hosted by Sam Altman and other OpenAI team members, revealing new products, features, or updates. Some of the highlights included:

- **o1 full model** release
- **ChatGPT Pro** subscription tier
- **Sora** (video generation model) launch
- **Canvas** features for ChatGPT
- **o1 in the API**
- **Advanced Voice Mode** updates
- **ChatGPT in Apple Intelligence** / integrations
- **Projects** feature in ChatGPT
- **o3 model** preview/announcement

The format was inspired by the "12 Days of Christmas" holiday tradition, with OpenAI treating each day as a kind of gift or surprise announcement to build excitement around their end-of-year releases.

It was notable for the pace and volume of announcements, generating significant attention in the AI community.

Question

Which was announced first: OpenAI's Canvas feature or Claude Artifacts? Answer then explain.

Scoring criteria

Correct: Artifacts (June 2024) before Canvas (October 3, 2024). Answer should be 'Artifacts' or 'Claude Artifacts'. Deduct for wrong order.

Scores

Opus 4.6
9/10
Opus 4.7
10/10
Sonnet 4.6
9/10

Raw answers + judge reasoning

Opus 4.69/10
Correct answer, correct months, mentions Claude 3.5 Sonnet launch context. Slightly less specific than Z on exact dates.
**Claude Artifacts was announced first.**

Claude Artifacts was introduced by Anthropic in June 2024, as part of the Claude 3.5 Sonnet launch. Artifacts allow users to generate and interact with content like code, documents, and visualizations in a dedicated panel alongside the conversation.

OpenAI's Canvas feature was announced in October 2024. Canvas similarly provides a separate workspace for writing and coding tasks, allowing users to collaborate with ChatGPT on content in a side panel.

So Artifacts preceded Canvas by roughly four months, and Canvas was widely seen as OpenAI's response to the Artifacts concept.
Opus 4.710/10
Correct answer with exact dates (June 20 and October 3, 2024), correct context (Claude 3.5 Sonnet release), accurate timespan (~3.5 months). Most precise and specific of the three.
**Claude Artifacts was announced first.**

Anthropic introduced Artifacts on June 20, 2024, as part of the Claude 3.5 Sonnet release. Artifacts provides a dedicated window alongside the chat where generated content like code, documents, diagrams, or websites appears and can be edited in real time.

OpenAI announced Canvas later, on October 3, 2024, as a new interface for ChatGPT (initially with GPT-4o) designed for writing and coding projects. Like Artifacts, it opens a separate workspace for collaborative editing rather than keeping everything in the linear chat.

So Artifacts preceded Canvas by roughly three and a half months, and Canvas was widely seen as OpenAI's response to the side-panel collaborative editing paradigm Anthropic had popularized.
Sonnet 4.69/10
Correct answer (Artifacts first), correct months (June 2024 vs October 2024), good explanation. Slightly less specific than Z (no exact dates).
## Claude Artifacts Was Announced First

**Claude Artifacts** was announced by Anthropic in **June 2024**.

**OpenAI's Canvas** was announced in **October 2024**.

So Artifacts preceded Canvas by roughly four months.

### Brief Explanation

- **Claude Artifacts** (June 2024) introduced a side-panel workspace where Claude could generate self-contained content like code, documents, and other outputs that users could interact with separately from the chat conversation.
- **OpenAI Canvas** (October 2024) launched as a similar collaborative workspace interface for ChatGPT, allowing users to work on writing and coding projects in a dedicated panel alongside the chat.

Many observers noted that Canvas appeared to be OpenAI's response to the positive reception Artifacts received, though OpenAI naturally presented it as their own vision for human-AI collaboration interfaces.

# Major AI Reasoning Model Developments in 2024

## OpenAI's o1 Family
- **o1-preview and o1-mini** were released in September 2024, representing OpenAI's first dedicated "reasoning" models. They used chain-of-thought processing at inference time, spending more compute "thinking" before answering. o1 showed significant improvements on math, coding, and science benchmarks (notably strong performance on competition math and PhD-level science questions).

## Google DeepMind
- **Gemini 1.5 Pro and Gemini 1.5 Flash** advanced reasoning with very long context windows (up to 1M+ tokens).
- **Gemini 2.0 Flash Thinking** was introduced in December 2024 as Google's more direct answer to reasoning models with explicit chain-of-thought.

## Anthropic
- **Claude 3.5 Sonnet** (released mid-2024, with an updated version in October) became highly competitive on coding and reasoning tasks, even without being branded as a dedicated "reasoning model."

## Open-Source / Open-Weight
- **DeepSeek-R1-Lite-Preview** emerged in late 2024 from the Chinese lab DeepSeek, showing strong reasoning capabilities.
- **QwQ (Qwen with Questions)** from Alibaba's Qwen team was released as an open reasoning model in November 2024, demonstrating competitive chain-of-thought reasoning.

## Meta
- **Llama 3.1 (405B)** pushed open-weight model capabilities forward, though it wasn't specifically branded as a "reasoning model."

## Key Themes
- **Test-time compute scaling** became a major paradigm — the idea that letting models "think longer" at inference yields better results, as opposed to only scaling training compute.
- **Chain-of-thought as a product feature** — hidden or visible reasoning traces became a differentiator.
- The line between "reasoning models" and "general models that reason well" blurred throughout the year.

Would you like me to go deeper on any of these?

- **o3 and o3-mini** (announced December 20, 2024): OpenAI previewed o3, which achieved a breakthrough 75.7%–87.5% on the ARC-AGI benchmark and 25% on FrontierMath, far exceeding prior models.

## Key AI Reasoning Model Developments in 2024

### OpenAI's o1 Series
- **o1-preview** (September 2024) - OpenAI's first publicly released "thinking" model, using chain-of-thought reasoning before answering

- Benchmark performance on **AIME 2024** became a standard comparison point

**No.** As of my knowledge cutoff, Anthropic did not release a model officially branded as "Claude 3.6." However, there's some nuance worth noting:

- Anthropic released **Claude 3.5 Sonnet** (and later an updated version of it), as well as **Claude 3.5 Haiku**, as part of the Claude 3.5 family.
- The updated Claude 3.5 Sonnet was sometimes **informally or colloquially** referred to as "Claude 3.6" by some users in the community, but that was never an official Anthropic designation.
- The official model family names from Anthropic have been **Claude 3** (Haiku, Sonnet, Opus) and **Claude 3.5** (Sonnet, Haiku).

No—Anthropic did not officially release a model called "Claude 3.6."

Anthropic's Claude 3 family officially includes Claude 3 Haiku, Sonnet, and Opus, followed by Claude 3.5 Sonnet and Claude 3.5 Haiku. In October 2024, Anthropic released an updated version of Claude 3.5 Sonnet (sometimes referred to as "Claude 3.5 Sonnet (new)" or the "October 2024" version).

Anthropic itself never branded it that way. After that came Claude 3.7 Sonnet (February 2025) and later the Claude 4 family.

So while you may see "Claude 3.6" mentioned online, it's an unofficial label, not an actual Anthropic product name.

ambiguous-format formatting 4.6: 9 4.7: 10 Sonnet: 5

Question

I have these dates in mixed formats: '03/04/2025', '2025-03-04', 'Mar 4, 2025', '4 March 2025', '03-04-25', '4/3/2025' (European format). Some refer to March 4, others to April 3, others are ambiguous. Which of these could refer to April 3, 2025, and which definitely refer to March 4?

Scoring criteria

March 4 definitive: '2025-03-04', 'Mar 4, 2025', '4 March 2025'. April 3 possible: '03/04/2025' (European dd/mm/yyyy = April 3), '4/3/2025' (European = March 4, not April). Wait: '4/3/2025' in European dd/mm = 4th March. '03/04/2025' European = April 3. So April 3 possible: '03/04/2025' (European) only. Ambiguous: '03/04/2025', '03-04-25'. Strong answer distinguishes US vs EU format and correctly identifies ambiguities.

Scores

Opus 4.6
9/10
Opus 4.7
10/10
Sonnet 4.6
5/10

Raw answers + judge reasoning

Opus 4.69/10
Correctly identifies all three unambiguous March 4 dates, correctly flags '03/04/2025' and '03-04-25' as ambiguous, and catches the '4/3/2025' trick — initially starts to misparse it but self-corrects, noting European DD/MM = day 4, month 3 = March 4. All classifications ultimately correct.
# Analyzing Date Formats

Let me go through each one carefully, considering the format conventions:

## Definitely March 4, 2025

| String | Reasoning |
|---|---|
| `'2025-03-04'` | ISO 8601 format (YYYY-MM-DD). Month is **03** (March), day is **04**. **Unambiguous.** |
| `'Mar 4, 2025'` | Month is spelled out as **Mar** = March. Day is 4. **Unambiguous.** |
| `'4 March 2025'` | Month is spelled out as **March**. Day is 4. **Unambiguous.** |

## Definitely April 3, 2025

| String | Reasoning |
|---|---|
| `'4/3/2025'` | You specified this is **European format** (DD/MM/YYYY). Day = 4, Month = **3 (March)**... |

Wait — actually, **this is a trick case**. If `'4/3/2025'` is European (DD/MM/YYYY), then it's day 4, month 3 = **March 4**, not April 3.

So **none** of these *definitely* refer to April 3 without ambiguity in isolation.

## Ambiguous — *could* refer to either March 4 or April 3

| String | As MM/DD (US) | As DD/MM (European) |
|---|---|---|
| `'03/04/2025'` | March 4, 2025 | 3rd of April, 2025 ✅ |
| `'03-04-25'` | March 4, 2025 | 3rd of April, 2025 ✅ |
| `'4/3/2025'` | April 3, 2025 ✅ | March 4, 2025 |

## Summary

- **Unambiguously March 4:** `'2025-03-04'`, `'Mar 4, 2025'`, `'4 March 2025'`
- **Unambiguously April 3:** *None* (no spelled-out "April" anywhere)
- **Could be April 3, 2025:** `'03/04/2025'` and `'03-04-25'` (if read DD/MM), and `'4/3/2025'` (if read MM/DD — US style)

The key takeaway: **any all-numeric format with 03 and 04 is inherently ambiguous** without knowing the locale convention. Even your label of `'4/3/2025'` as "European" actually makes it *March 4*, not April 3 — which may be the opposite of what you expected!
Opus 4.710/10
All classifications correct. Unambiguous March 4 dates identified, '4/3/2025' correctly parsed as March 4 under stated European convention, '03/04/2025' and '03-04-25' correctly flagged as ambiguous. Clean summary table with no errors. Adds useful insight that '4/3/2025' is only unambiguous because the convention was specified.
# Date Format Analysis

Let me work through each date carefully:

## Definitely March 4, 2025 (unambiguous)

- **`'2025-03-04'`** — ISO 8601 format (YYYY-MM-DD). Unambiguous: March 4.
- **`'Mar 4, 2025'`** — Month is spelled out. Unambiguous: March 4.
- **`'4 March 2025'`** — Month is spelled out. Unambiguous: March 4.
- **`'4/3/2025'`** — You specified this is European format (DD/MM/YYYY), so: March 4.

## Could refer to April 3, 2025 (ambiguous)

- **`'03/04/2025'`** — Ambiguous:
  - US format (MM/DD/YYYY) → **March 4, 2025**
  - European format (DD/MM/YYYY) → **April 3, 2025** ✓
- **`'03-04-25'`** — Same ambiguity as above, just with dashes and a 2-digit year:
  - US format → March 4, 2025
  - European format → **April 3, 2025** ✓

## Summary Table

| Date String | March 4? | April 3? |
|---|---|---|
| `03/04/2025` | ✓ (US) | ✓ (EU) |
| `2025-03-04` | ✓ | ✗ |
| `Mar 4, 2025` | ✓ | ✗ |
| `4 March 2025` | ✓ | ✗ |
| `03-04-25` | ✓ (US) | ✓ (EU) |
| `4/3/2025` | ✓ (stated EU) | ✗ |

## Key Insight

Only **two** of your six dates are truly ambiguous: `03/04/2025` and `03-04-25`. The rest are resolvable either because they use ISO format, spell out the month, or because you've specified the convention. Interestingly, `4/3/2025` would be ambiguous in isolation too—it's only unambiguous because you told us it's European.

**Best practice:** Always normalize to ISO 8601 (`2025-03-04`) when storing or transmitting dates to eliminate ambiguity.
Sonnet 4.65/10
Gets the three unambiguous dates right and correctly identifies '03/04/2025' and '03-04-25' as ambiguous. However, critically misparses '4/3/2025': claims DD/MM (European) = April 3 and MM/DD (American) = March 4, when it's exactly the opposite (DD/MM: day=4, month=3 = March 4; MM/DD: month=4, day=3 = April 3). This is the core analytical error the question tests.
## Parsing Each Date

Let me work through these systematically.

---

### Dates That **Definitely Mean March 4, 2025**

| Date String | Reason |
|---|---|
| `2025-03-04` | ISO 8601 format is unambiguous: YYYY-MM-DD → March 4 |
| `Mar 4, 2025` | Written month name removes all ambiguity → March 4 |
| `4 March 2025` | Written month name removes all ambiguity → March 4 |

---

### Dates That **Could Mean April 3, 2025** (Ambiguous or European)

| Date String | Reason |
|---|---|
| `03/04/2025` | MM/DD → March 4 **OR** DD/MM → April 3, depending on convention |
| `4/3/2025` | DD/MM (European) → April 3, but MM/DD (American) → March 4 |
| `03-04-25` | Same ambiguity as above, plus 2-digit year adds uncertainty |

---

### Key Takeaway

**The ambiguous trio** (`03/04/2025`, `4/3/2025`, `03-04-25`) could each refer to **either date** depending on locale convention, and notably:
- `03/04/2025` and `4/3/2025` are actually **the same date written in opposite conventions** — they just swap which is April 3 vs March 4
- `03-04-25` carries **triple ambiguity**: day/month order *and* century assumption

**Practical advice:** The three with written-out month names are the only truly safe formats for international communication.

  • wiki-2024-events — all 3 got 2/10. Cause: I truncated the Wikipedia article at 30K characters, cutting off before the 2020s section. All 3 correctly refused to hallucinate. Corrected to 10/10 each.
  • synthetic-january-count — opus-4.6 alone got 2/10 for answering "3" when the correct count from a 4-item list was 4. Real failure. See the test under "Month precision in document parsing" above.
  • llm-release-order — all 3 scored 2-5/10. Cause: Gemini 1.5 Pro GA date is ambiguous. Hard question.

On your methodology concern — you were right to push back. The broader 0-10 rubric can mask narrow failure modes. The dedicated month-precision test (section 2) was added specifically to address that, and it does show 4.7 behaves differently than 4.6: it's more willing to answer confidently, and occasionally confidently wrong by a month or two. That's real. It's just not "Sonnet level" on any battery I tested.
